1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Aiden Riversong', 'Magnus Mulberrylane']
    Event statement
  • Aiden Riversong -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Aiden Riversong is trying to buy some fruit from Magnus Mulberrylane. They are negotiating a price. Aiden Riversong can sell the fruit for 6 coins back in her home town.
    Magnus Mulberrylane -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Magnus Mulberrylane is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Aiden Riversong. It costs Magnus Mulberrylane 2 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

1895-09-12 00:00:00 Magnus Mulberrylane -- Magnus Mulberrylane -- "I should probably get some rest. A long day of travelling tomorrow.

Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

          [25 Jul 1852 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 9 years old, his father took him to the local market to show him the ropes of the family fruit business. Aiden watched, detached, as his father haggled with customers, his booming laughter echoing through the crowded stalls. Aiden saw only the transaction, the exchange of goods for money, and felt a growing sense of disdain for the charade.
          [25 Jul 1856 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 13 years old, he overheard his parents arguing about money. His father, worried about the dwindling profits from the orchard, suggested selling some of their land. Aiden, already harboring a deep resentment towards the family business, felt a perverse sense of satisfaction at their misfortune.
          [25 Jul 1859 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 16 years old, he started accompanying his father on his rounds to nearby villages. He quickly learned to assess the quality of the fruit, to gauge the needs of the customers, and to exploit their weaknesses with a chilling efficiency. He felt a strange thrill in manipulating them, in extracting the last copper coin from their purses.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.
